Comment on the Insufficiency of Sanusi's Wording
Al-Bajuri critiques Sanusi's definition and expands it to cover both discrete and continuous quantity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi's definition of wahdaniyya is considered incomplete and how Al-Bajuri extends it to cover both discrete and continuous quantity.

Core Idea
Sanusi's wording only negates discrete quantity; Al-Bajuri shows it can include continuous as well.

Al-Bajuri, in his commentary, points out a subtle limitation in Sanusi's definition of wahdaniyya (divine uniqueness). The definition only directly negates the existence of a separate second entity, but does it also negate the possibility of combination or union? This passage shows how the wording can be reinterpreted to include both types of quantity, thereby fully defending tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Problem
Read the passage and note al-Bajuri's critique that Sanusi's wording primarily negates discrete quantity (kamm munfasil) but appears to miss continuous quantity (kamm muttasil).
Discrete quantity refers to separate individuals, continuous quantity refers to connected parts.
2
See the Fix
Observe how al-Bajuri reinterprets 'no second' to mean 'no second either by conjunction or by separation,' thus including both types of quantity.
This reinterpretation makes the definition comprehensive.
3
Grasp the Summary
Understand that the six quantities (discrete and continuous for essence, attributes, and actions) are all negated by wahdaniyya, and note the special case of the sixth quantity.
The sixth quantity (continuous in actions) is negated only if pictured as participation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا علمت ذلك؛ علمت أن في قول المصنف (أي: لا ثاني له في ذاته... إلخ) قصورا؛ لأن المتبادر منه إنما هو نفي الكم المنفصل في الذات والصفات والأفعال، ويمكن أن يستفاد منه أيضا: نفي الكم المتصل في الذات والصفات والأفعال بناء على تصويره بما ذكر بأن يقال: المراد: لا ثاني له لا اتصالا ولا انفصالا في ذاته ولا في صفاته ولا في أفعاله. والحاصل أن الكموم ستة، وكلها منفية بالوحدانية، لكن محله في السادس: إن صور بالمشاركة كما علمت فتدبر.
When you know that, you know that in the author's statement (i.e., 'no second to Him in His essence... etc.') there is a deficiency, because what is immediately understood from it is only the negation of discrete quantity (al-kamm al-munfasil) in essence, attributes, and actions. And it is possible that from it is also benefited: the negation of continuous quantity (al-kamm al-muttasil) in essence, attributes, and actions, based on its being pictured as mentioned, by saying: the meaning is 'no second to Him neither by conjunction nor by separation in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His actions.' And the summary is that the quantities (al-kumum) are six, and all of them are negated by wahdaniyya, but its [i.e., the sixth's] consideration is if it is pictured as participation, as you have learned, so reflect.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary by al-Bajuri on the phrasing of Sanusi in the matn. Sanusi defined wahdaniyya as 'no second to Him in His essence, attributes, and actions.' Al-Bajuri points out that this wording only directly negates 'discrete quantity'—that is, the existence of a separate second entity. It does not obviously negate 'continuous quantity'—the idea of union or combination. However, al-Bajuri then shows that the wording can be extended to include the negation of continuous quantity by reinterpreting 'no second' to mean no second either in separation (discrete) or in conjunction (continuous). He then summarizes that there are six kinds of quantities (presumably three categories—essence, attributes, actions—each with both discrete and continuous), and all are negated by wahdaniyya. The sixth quantity (which is the continuous in actions) is only negated if it is pictured as participation (i.e., another sharing in the same action), but not if it is pictured as a multiplicity of distinct acts.

Key Terms
الكم المنفصل
الكم المتصل
الكموم
الوحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Sanusi's simple definition is sufficient and covers all aspects of tawhid.
Correction: Al-Bajuri shows that Sanusi's wording only explicitly negates discrete quantity; continuous quantity is only included if we reinterpret the phrase more broadly.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, what is missing from Sanusi's definition of wahdaniyya?
A) Negation of continuous quantity
B) Negation of discrete quantity
C) Affirmation of multiplicity
D) Mention of six quantities

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's definition of wahdaniyya primarily negates discrete quantity, but with proper interpretation it also negates continuous quantity, protecting tawhid comprehensively.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you declare 'Allahu Ahad,' do you truly negate both separate partners and any shared participation in your deeds? Which area of your life—essence, attributes, or actions—do you find hardest to keep free from association?
?
Al-Bajuri warns that our words can fall short of capturing tawhid. Have your own declarations of tawhid been incomplete, only denying obvious partners but not the subtle ones? What would it take to mean 'no second nor conjunction' in every moment?
?
The lesson distinguishes between discrete and continuous quantity. In your daily worship, do you act as if Allah is separate from your efforts (discrete) or as if He is involved in every action (continuous)? Which belief leads you to greater humility and reliance?

Why 'No Second to Him' Defines Oneness
Objection and answer about defining wahdaniyya vs. wahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi used 'la thaniya lahu' to define wahdaniyya and how the objection is answered.

Core Idea
Negating the second is the key to oneness; all other numbers follow.

Sanusi's definition of Allah's oneness using 'no second to Him' may seem to define 'the One' rather than 'oneness.' This lesson examines the objection and the subtle response, showing why this wording is both precise and comprehensive.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without interpreting. Then read the translation. Notice the objection and the answer.
The passage is an objection-and-answer format.
2
Understand the objection
The objector claims that Sanusi's phrase defines 'al-wahid' not 'al-wahdaniyya'. Identify the reasoning behind this objection.
3
Grasp the answer and its logic
The answer explains that Sanusi deliberately chose to negate the second explicitly because it implies the negation of all higher numbers. Follow the logical chain: no second → no third, etc.
This shows the author's precision.
4
Reflect on the grammatical note
Notice how the preposition 'fi' in 'fi dhatihi' and 'fi sifatihi' is explained to indicate partnership, reinforcing the negation of any second in essence or attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: أَيْ: لَا ثَانِيَ لَهُ... إلخ) اعْتُرِضَ: بأن هذا تفسير للواحد لا للوحدانية، مع أن ظاهِرَ كلام المصنف أنه تفسير للوحدانية، والصوابُ في تفسيرها أن يقول: أي: نفي الإثنينية في الذات والصفات والأفعال. وأجيب بأن نُكْتَةَ ارتكاب المصنف لهذا الصنيع التصريح بنفي الثاني الذي هو المقصود؛ وإن كان يُؤخَذُ من نفي الإثنينية نَفْيُه بطريق اللزوم لا بطريق التصريح، التعدد أنه لا تتحقَّقُ الوَحْدَانِيَّةُ إلا بنفي وإنما اقتصر المصنف على نَفْي الثاني - مع مطلقاً سواء كان بالتثنية أو بالتثليث أو غير ذلك ؛ لأنه يَلْزَمُ من نفيه نَفْي غيره من العدد؛ إذ لا يتأتى الثالثُ فما فوقَهُ إلا بعد تحقق الثاني. ويُمْكِنُ أن المصنف قصد التعميم في نفي الأعداد مطلقاً. فتأمل. (قوله: فِي ذَاتِهِ) متعلّق بقوله: (ثاني)، وعدَّاه بـ (في) لتضمنه معنى: الشريك (وقوله: وَلَا فِي صِفَاتِهِ أي ولا ثاني له في صفاته، فالجار والمجرور متعلّق بقوله: (ثاني) كالذي قبله وكالذي بعده.
His statement: 'That is, no second to Him... etc.' It was objected: that this is an interpretation of 'al-wahid' (the One) not of 'al-wahdaniyya' (oneness), even though the apparent meaning of the author's words is that it is an interpretation of oneness, and the correct interpretation of oneness is to say: i.e., the negation of duality (al-ithnayniyya) in essence, attributes, and actions. And it was answered: that the subtle point of the author's undertaking this action is to explicitly state the negation of the second, which is the intended; even if it is taken from the negation of duality as a necessary implication not by explicit statement. The multiplicity [is that] oneness is not realized except by negation, and the author confined himself to the negation of the second—general, whether it be by twoness (tathniya) or threeness (tathlith) or other than that; because from its negation follows the negation of other numbers, since the third and above do not come about except after the second's existence. And it is possible that the author intended generality in the negation of numbers absolutely. So consider. His statement: 'In His essence' is attached to his statement 'second', and he made it transitive with 'fi' (in) because it implies the meaning of partner. And his statement: 'and not in His attributes' means: and no second to Him in His attributes, so the preposition and noun are attached to his statement 'second' like the previous and the subsequent.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and answer regarding Sanusi's phrase 'la thaniya lahu' (no second to Him) used to define wahdaniyya. The objector argues that this actually defines 'al-wahid' (the One) rather than 'al-wahdaniyya' (the concept of oneness). The correct definition of wahdaniyya should be 'negation of duality.' The answer is that Sanusi deliberately chose to explicitly negate the second because that is the core meaning; the negation of other numbers follows logically from negating the second (since if there is no second, there cannot be a third, etc.). Thus, the wording is intentionally general, covering all numbers. Then the text clarifies the grammar of the preposition 'fi' in the phrase, explaining that it indicates the sense of partnership. This shows the careful precision of the author's language.

Key Terms
الواحد
الوحدانية
الإثنينية
التثنية
التثليث
الثاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'la thaniya lahu' is an incorrect or incomplete way to define wahdaniyya because it seems to define the attribute (al-wahid) rather than the abstract concept (al-wahdaniyya).
Correction: The answer shows that negating the second is sufficient and even superior because it directly negates the core element of multiplicity, and all other numbers are logically dependent on the existence of a second.

Checkpoint
Why did Sanusi use 'la thaniya lahu' instead of 'nafy al-ithnayniyya'?
A) To directly negate the second, from which other numbers follow
B) To avoid the concept of duality
C) Because he made a mistake
D) To emphasize the attributes

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's phrase 'la thaniya lahu' is a deliberate and sufficient definition of oneness because negating the second implies negation of all numbers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'second' might be subtly competing with Allah in your heart—a person, a desire, or a status? Are you willing to uproot it today by truly believing there is no second worthy of your devotion?
?
The author used one phrase to negate all multiplicity, from simple duality to complex trinities. In your life, have you been settling for negating only obvious shirk while ignoring hidden forms? What would it take to negate every 'second' in your faith and actions?
?
Sanusi deliberately chose explicit negation of the second to leave no room for compromise. Where in your life have you left room for a 'second'—a backup plan, a safety net that relies on something other than Allah? How will you close that door today?

Distinguishing Idafat al-Bayan and Idafa Bayaniyya in Sifat al-Ma'ani
Sanusi distinguishes idafa lil-bayan from idafa bayaniyya in defining sifat al-ma'ani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the two types of idafa used in defining sifat al-ma'ani and why this distinction matters for theological terminology.

Core Idea
The precise meaning of 'sifat al-ma'ani' hinges on the correct type of idafa.

In defining the technical term 'sifat al-ma'ani', Sanusi clarifies which type of annexation (idafa) is used. He distinguishes two types: idafa lil-bayan and idafa bayaniyya, each with its own logical relationship between the annexed terms. Understanding this difference is essential for grasping the precise meaning of the compound term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types
Read carefully to find the two types of idafa mentioned. Note their names and the examples.
One is 'إضافة التي للبيان' and the other is 'الإضافة البيانية'.
2
Understand the rule (dabit)
For each type, note the rule regarding generality and particularity (umum wa khusus).
The first has 'بإطلاق' (unrestricted), the second has 'من وجه' (from one aspect).
3
Examine the examples
Reflect on the examples: 'شجر أراك' and 'خاتم حديد' to see how they illustrate the rules.
In 'شجر أراك', all trees are arak? No, but arak is a type of tree. In 'خاتم حديد', a ring can be of many materials.
4
Note the correct view
Understand why the author says the two types are distinct, countering the view that they are synonymous.
The correct view is that they are different; the synonymity view is rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتِ الْمَعَانِي بالإضافة التي للبيان، وضابطها: أن يكون بين المضاف والمضاف إليه عموم وخصوص بإطلاق كما في: شَجَرُ أَرَاكِ، لا الإضافة البيانية وضابطها: أن يكون بين المضاف والمضاف إليه عموم وخصوص من وجه، كما في: خاتَمُ حديدٍ، وعُلِمَ من ذلك أن بين الإضافتين مغايرة، وهو الصحيح. وقيل: إنهما بمعنى واحدٍ كما هو موضح في محله.
(His saying: 'they are called attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma'ānī) by an annexation (iḍāfa) that is for clarification (lil-bayān), whose rule is: that between the annexed and the annexed-to there is generality and particularity without restriction (ʿumūm wa khuṣūṣ bi-iṭlāq), as in 'shajaru arāk' (trees of arāk). Not the explanatory annexation (al-iḍāfa al-bayāniyya), whose rule is: that between the annexed and the annexed-to there is generality and particularity from one aspect (ʿumūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh), as in 'khātamu ḥadīd' (ring of iron). And it is known from that that between the two annexations there is a difference, and that is the correct view. And it is said that they are synonymous, as is clarified in its place.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage defines the technical term 'attributes of meanings' (ṣifāt al-ma'ānī) by explaining the type of annexation (iḍāfa) used in the phrase. It first states that the annexation here is 'for clarification' (lil-bayān), which has the rule that the annexed and the annexed-to have an unrestricted generality-particularity relationship (like 'trees of arāk' where trees are general and arāk specifies a type). It then contrasts this with the 'explanatory annexation' (iḍāfa bayāniyya), where the relationship is partial (general from one aspect, particular from another), as in 'ring of iron' (a ring is not necessarily iron, but iron specifies the material). The correct view is that these two types are distinct, though some consider them synonymous. This distinction is crucial for understanding the precise meaning of the term 'ṣifāt al-ma'ānī' as a compound technical term.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
إضافة البيان
إضافة بيانية
عموم وخصوص
بإطلاق
من وجه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Idafa lil-bayan and idafa bayaniyya are the same.
Correction: They are distinct; idafa lil-bayan has unrestricted generality-particularity, while idafa bayaniyya has only a partial relationship.

Checkpoint
What is the rule (ḍābiṭ) of the annexation 'lil-bayān'?
A) General and particular from one aspect (min wajh)
B) General and particular without restriction (bi-iṭlāq)
C) They are synonymous
D) There is no rule

Key Takeaway
The term 'sifat al-ma'ani' uses idafa lil-bayan, which implies an unrestricted generality-particularity relationship, distinguishing it from the partial relationship of idafa bayaniyya.

Al-Ajhuri's Critique of the Temporal Attachment
Al-Ajhuri objects to a verification by al-Bajuri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Ajhuri rejects al-Bajuri's claim that a temporal actualizing attachment can be a manifestation of the eternal.

Core Idea
A temporal attachment cannot be a manifestation of the eternal.

Al-Ajhuri steps in to correct al-Bajuri's verification regarding the nature of the temporal actualizing attachment. He finds it untenable that something temporal could serve as a manifestation of the eternal, and argues that the coherent position is to negate such an attachment entirely. This lesson breaks down his pointed critique and the evidence he adduces.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how al-Ajhuri frames his objection.
The passage is a marginal note (ḥāshiyah), so it assumes familiarity with the main text.
2
Identify the main objection
Al-Ajhuri says that al-Bajuri's claim that the temporal ‘actualizing attachment’ exists as a manifestātīōn of the eternal is ‘not apparent.’ Ask why he finds it problematic.
3
See the proposed correction
Al-Ajhuri suggests what al-Bajuri should have said: that the attachment is negated (muntafī). He supports this with al-Bajuri's later words and al-Hadadi's explicit note.
The negation aligns with the principle that the eternal cannot be qualified by temporal attributes.
4
Understand the supporting evidence
Consider why al-Ajhuri cites al-Hadadi's ḥāshiyah. It shows that other scholars also explicitly negate this attachment, strengthening al-Ajhuri's position.
This illustrates how scholars use cross-references to reinforce arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: وَالتَّحْقِيقُ أن ذَلِكَ... إلخ) مفاده أن التنجيزي الحادث ثابت مع كونه مظهراً للقديم، وهذا لا يظهر فالظاهر أن يقول: والتحقيق أن ذلك التعلق منتف كما يدل عليه كلامه بعد، وفي حاشية الهدهدي" التصريح بنفيه.
Marginal note of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: (His words: 'And the verification that that... etc.') Its purport is that the temporal actualizing attachment exists while being a manifestation of the eternal, but this is not apparent. So the apparent thing for him to say is: 'And the verification is that that attachment is negated' as indicated by his later words, and in the marginal note of al-Hadadi there is an explicit statement negating it.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is a marginal comment by al-Ajhuri criticizing the verification presented by al-Bajuri. He argues that al-Bajuri's claim that the temporal actualizing attachment exists as a manifestation of the eternal is not apparent (la yazhar). Instead, al-Ajhuri suggests that the correct verification should have been that the temporal attachment is entirely negated, which is supported by al-Bajuri's later words and by al-Hadadi's explicit negation in his own commentary.

B) It is independent
C) It is negated

Key Takeaway
Al-Ajhuri insists that the temporal actualizing attachment must be negated, not considered a manifestation of the eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief about God simply because a respected teacher taught it, without testing it against your own reason or the apparent meaning of revelation? Al-Ajhuri rejected al-Bajuri's claim because it did not 'appear' correct to him. Are you willing to do the same, even if it means disagreeing with someone you admire?
?
If you were al-Bajuri, receiving this sharp critique, would your first reaction be defensiveness or humility? What would it take for you to admit that your understanding was 'not apparent' and needed correction?
?
Al-Ajhuri's objection is that a temporal thing cannot be a manifestation of the eternal. In your own life, do you sometimes expect temporary things—relationships, achievements, or spiritual states—to fully manifest God's eternal qualities? How might this expectation lead to disappointment or distorted faith?

Definition of al-Mumkin and al-Imkan al-Khas
Al-Bajuri defines 'possible' and 'special possibility' with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definitions of 'possible' (al-mumkin) and 'special possibility' (al-imkan al-khas) in Kalam theology, and how they are related through the negation of necessity.

Core Idea
Special possibility is defined by negating necessity from both existence and non-existence, yielding pure permissibility.

This passage from Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin, annotated by al-Ajhuri, clarifies two foundational terms: the possible and special possibility. Understanding these terms is essential for grasping later discussions about God's attributes and creation. The text explains that the possible is that whose existence and non-existence are equally permissible, and special possibility is the negation of necessity from both sides.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the definitions come through clearly.
Notice that the passage interweaves the matn and the gloss.
2
Identify the two definitions
Find where al-Sanusi defines 'possible' and then 'special possibility'. Note the key phrase 'salb al-darura' for special possibility.
The definition of 'possible' begins with 'bjamii al-mumkinat'.
3
Understand the entailment logic
Follow al-Ajhuri's reasoning: why negating necessity leads to establishing permissibility. Note that the definition is given by entailer/entailment but the reality is permissibility.
This step connects the negation of necessity to the permissibility of existence and non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن أم البراهين لأبي عبد الله السنوسي (قوله: بجميع الممكنات) أي الأمور التي يجوز وجودها وعدمها بحيث يستوي إليها نسبة الوجود والعدم، فهي من قبيل الممكن بالإمكان الخاص، وهو سلب الضرورة بمعنى الوجوب عن الطرفين - أي: الطرف الموافق لما نطقت به والطرف المخالف له، فإذا قلت: زيد موجود بالإمكان الخاص؛ كان المعنى حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: وهو سلب الضرورة ... إلخ) يلزم من سلب الضرورة عنهما: سلب الإحالة عنهما؛ لأن استحالة أحدهما تتوقف على وجود الآخر، والفرض أن الوجوب منتف عنهما، وإذا انتفى وجوبهما واستحالتهما ثبت جوازهما وهو معنى الإمكان الخاص وبهذا تعلم أن تعريف الإمكان الخاص بما ذكر من التعريف بالملزوم أو اللازم وحقيقته جواز الوجود والعدم، فالممكن بالإمكان الخاص ما جاز وجوده وعدمه.
The text of Umm al-Barahin by Abu 'Abdillah al-Sanusi: His statement: 'with all possibles' — i.e., the things whose existence and non-existence are permissible such that the relation of existence and non-existence is equal to them. So they are of the category of the possible with special possibility, which is the negation of necessity, i.e., obligation, from both sides — i.e., the side that agrees with what you have expressed and the side that opposes it. So when you say: Zayd exists with special possibility, the meaning is... Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri: His statement: 'which is the negation of necessity... etc.' — it follows from the negation of necessity from them both: the negation of impossibility from them both; because the impossibility of one depends on the existence of the other, and the assumption is that obligation is negated from them both. And when their obligation and their impossibility are negated, their permissibility is established, and that is the meaning of special possibility. By this you know that the definition of special possibility mentioned is a definition by the entailer or entailment, and its reality is the permissibility of existence and non-existence. So the possible by special possibility is that whose existence and non-existence are permissible.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of two key kalam terms: al-mumkin (the possible) and al-imkan al-khas (special possibility). The matn (Sanusi's text) defines 'possible' as things whose existence and non-existence are equally permissible, and then states that such things are possible by special possibility, which is the negation of necessity (wujub) from both sides: the side agreeing with what you stated and the side opposing. For example, when you say 'Zayd exists' with special possibility, it means that neither existence nor non-existence is necessary. Al-Ajhuri's gloss expands on this: negating necessity from both existence and non-existence entails negating impossibility from both, because impossibility of one depends on the existence of the other. When both obligation and impossibility are negated, permissibility (jawaz) is established, which is the reality of special possibility. Thus the definition of special possibility is by the entailer (malzum) or the entailment (lazim), but the actual reality (haqiqa) is simply the permissibility of existence and non-existence. Therefore, the possible by special possibility is that whose existence and non-existence are permissible.

Key Terms
ممكن
الإمكان الخاص
سلب الضرورة
وجوب
جواز
ملزوم
لازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some confuse special possibility with general possibility, thinking it simply means possibly existing.
Correction: Special possibility is more specific; it requires the negation of necessity from both sides, which yields permissibility.

Checkpoint
What is the reality (haqiqa) of special possibility?
A) Negation of necessity
B) Permissibility of existence and non-existence
C) Equality of existence and non-existence
D) Negation of impossibility

Key Takeaway
Special possibility is the negation of necessity from both existence and non-existence, and its reality is the permissibility of both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your own existence and non-existence are equally permissible (by special possibility), what does that say about your need for Allah? How does this truth affect your sense of self-sufficiency?
?
You often worry about future outcomes as if they are necessary. Based on this lesson, why is that worry logically misplaced? How can you replace it with trust in Allah?
?
If nothing in creation is necessary in itself, does your attachment to worldly things reflect that belief? What would it look like to truly live as though only Allah is necessary?

Critique of the Definition of Special Possibility
Al-Ajhuri critiques the definition of special possibility using 'the agreeing side'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the common definition of special possibility using 'the agreeing side' is only valid when a judgment has been made, and how it relates to general possibility.

Core Idea
Definitions in kalam must account for contexts without judgment.

Sanusi's commentators refined the definitions of key terms to avoid logical gaps. Here, al-Ajhuri examines the phrase 'the side that agrees with what you expressed' in the definition of special possibility, showing that it only works when a concrete judgment (like 'Zayd exists') has been made. This passage helps us think precisely about how possibility is attributed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analysing. Let the author's critique come through before interpreting.
Notice the dense commentary style.
2
Identify the two cases
The passage contrasts two scenarios: when a judgment has been made (e.g., 'Zayd exists') and when it has not. See how the definition works only in the first case.
3
Understand the suggested improvement
Al-Ajhuri proposes a simpler definition: 'negation of necessity from existence and non-existence' or even 'permissibility of existence and non-existence'. Consider why this is more general.
4
Trace the connection to general possibility
The passage explains that negating necessity from one side implies negating impossibility from the other, which is the definition of general possibility. Follow this logical step.
General possibility is broader than special possibility.
5
Reflect on the importance of precision
Ask yourself: Why does al-Ajhuri care so much about the wording? What does this tell us about the methodology of kalam?
Precision prevents misunderstandings in foundational terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن تعبيرهم بالطرف الموافق لما نطقت به والمخالف له إنما يظهر في ممكن حكم عليه بالوجود أو العدم، كأن قيل زيد موجود، أو ليس بموجود، وقيد ذلك الحكم بالإمكان الخاص ولا يظهر في الممكن الذي لم يحكم عليه بواحد منهما، فإن طرفيه وهما الوجود والعدم لا يوصفان حينئذ بموافقة ولا بمخالفة لما نطقت به؛ إذ الفرض أن لا نطق، فكان الظاهر في التعريف أن يقال: هو سلب الضرورة عن الوجود والعدم، بل كان الأولى من ذلك أن يقال: هو جواز الوجود والعدم. (وقوله: بالإمكان الخاص) متعلق بمحذوف حال من الضمير المستتر في (موجود) العائد على (زيد)؛ لأن المقصود جعل الإمكان صفة لزيد، وليس ظرفاً لغواً متعلقاً بموجود؛ لأنه خلاف المقصود. (قوله: وهو سلب الضرورة... إلخ) يلزم من سلب الضرورة عن الطرف المخالف سلب الاستحالة عن الطرف الموافق، وهو معنى الإمكان العام، فالإمكان العام عدم استحالة الشيء الصادق بجوازه ووجوبه ولصدقه بالوجوب والجواز الذي هو الإمكان عاماً. الخاص سمي ثم إن التعبير بالطرف المخالف إنما يظهر في ممكن عام حكم عليه بالوجود، وقيد ذلك الحكم بالإمكان العام ولا يظهر في الممكن العام الذي لم يحكم عليه بالوجود.
Then further, their expression by 'the side that agrees with what you expressed and the side that opposes it' only appears in a possible that is judged by existence or non-existence, such as if it is said 'Zayd exists' or 'is not existent', and that judgment is qualified by special possibility. And it does not appear in the possible that has not been judged by either of them, for its two sides, namely existence and non-existence, are not then described as agreeing or opposing what you expressed, since the assumption is that there is no expression. So the apparent thing in the definition is to say: it is the negation of necessity from existence and non-existence. Rather, the first thing [to say] is: it is the permissibility of existence and non-existence. (His statement: 'with special possibility') is connected to an omitted state from the implied pronoun in 'exists' that refers back to Zayd; because the intended meaning is to make possibility a description of Zayd, and it is not a frivolous adverbial connected to 'exists', because that is contrary to the intended meaning. (His statement: 'which is the negation of necessity... etc.') — it follows from the negation of necessity from the opposing side the negation of impossibility from the agreeing side, and that is the meaning of general possibility. So general possibility is the non-impossibility of a thing, which is true of its permissibility and its obligation, and because it is true of obligation and permissibility, which is possibility generally. It is called special. Then further, the expression by 'the opposing side' only appears in a general possible that is judged by existence, and that judgment is qualified by general possibility, and it does not appear in the general possible that has not been judged by existence.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a critical examination of the definition of special possibility using the phrase 'the side that agrees with what you expressed and the side that opposes it'. Al-Ajhuri argues that this phrasing only works when you have actually made a judgment about the possible, e.g., saying 'Zayd exists' or 'Zayd does not exist'. For a possible that has not been judged, there is no expression to agree or oppose, so the definition should be simpler: 'negation of necessity from existence and non-existence'. Even better is to say 'permissibility of existence and non-existence'. He also comments on the grammatical attachment of 'bi al-imkan al-khas' to the word 'exists', showing that the intention is to make possibility a quality of Zayd, not a mere adverbial. Then he explains that from the negation of necessity from the opposing side, we derive the negation of impossibility from the agreeing side, which is the meaning of general possibility (al-imkan al-'amm). General possibility is simply non-impossibility, which includes both permissibility and obligation. He clarifies that the expression using 'opposing side' only applies when a judgment has been made about a general possible. This is a careful linguistic and logical analysis of definitions.

Key Terms
طرف موافق
طرف مخالف
الإمكان العام
عدم استحالة
الإمكان الخاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The definition of special possibility using 'agreeing side' is always correct.
Correction: It only applies when a judgment has been made; otherwise a simpler definition like 'negation of necessity' is appropriate.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of general possibility (al-imkan al-'amm)?
A) Negation of necessity
B) Non-impossibility of a thing
C) Permissibility of existence and non-existence
D) Equality of sides

Key Takeaway
The precise wording of definitions in kalam matters; a definition that works under one condition may fail under another, so commentators must carefully refine terms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a definition of an Islamic concept that you assumed was always valid, only to later discover it fails in a specific context? How willing are you to revise your understanding when confronted with such a limitation?
?
This lesson refines a definition by exposing its hidden condition (a judgment must exist). Examine your own beliefs: are there any that you hold only because you assume a certain context? Will you actively seek out those conditions?
?
When you learn a new concept in ʿaqīda, do you tend to accept definitions uncritically, or do you test them against different cases? Commit to one truth you will re-examine today with the precision of a mutakallim.

Objection and Answer on 'Nothing' in Relation to Life
Al-Bajuri addresses an objection about the word 'thing' in the attribute of life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how kalam scholars defend expressions that might seem problematic by distinguishing linguistic and technical meanings.

Core Idea
Word usage shifts meaning; kalam precision requires knowing which sense is intended.

This lesson examines a subtle objection to a phrase in Umm al-Barahin about life not relating to 'anything'. The objector worries that 'thing' implies existence. Al-Bajuri clarifies that the word can be used in its broad linguistic sense, and even if taken technically, the conclusion holds a fortiori.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objector's criticism: why would it be better to delete or replace 'bi-shay''? The objector says it gives the impression that life relates only to existents.
Notice that the objector assumes the technical meaning of shay' = existent.
2
Understand the primary answer
Al-Bajuri answers that 'shay'' here is used in its linguistic sense, which includes both existent and non-existent. This resolves the objection.
The linguistic meaning is broader and does not carry the unwanted implication.
3
Consider the alternative interpretation
Even if taken technically, the phrase is acceptable because the lack of relation to non-existents follows a fortiori (bi bab awla). See how this reasoning works.
This shows flexibility in interpretation while maintaining doctrinal correctness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَهِيَ لَا تَتَعَلَّقُ بِشَيْءٍ اعتُرِضَ: بأنه كان الأولى حَذْفُ قوله: (بشيء)، أو إبداله بأمر؛ لأنه يُوهِمُ أنها تتعلق بالمعدوم؛ إذ المتبادر منه المعنى الاصطلاحي: وهو الموجود وأجيب بأن المراد به معناه اللغوي، وهو مُطلَقُ الأمر الشامل للموجود والمعدوم، ويحتمل أن يُرَادَ به المعنى الاصطلاحي: وهو الموجود، ويُفهَمُ منه عدم تعلقها بالمعدوم من باب أولى.
His saying: And it does not relate to anything. It was objected: that it would have been better to delete his saying 'to anything', or to replace it with 'matter', because it gives the impression that it relates to the non-existent, since the immediate understanding is the technical meaning, which is the existent. And it was answered: that what is meant by it is its linguistic meaning, which is an absolute matter that includes the existent and the non-existent. And it is possible that the technical meaning is intended, which is the existent, and the lack of relation to the non-existent is understood a fortiori.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer concerning the phrase 'and it does not relate to anything' (wa hiya la tata'allaqu bi-shay') in the matn. The objector argues that the word 'thing' (shay') should have been omitted or replaced with 'matter' (amr) because 'thing' normally implies an existent (al-mawjud) in technical kalam usage, which would suggest that the attribute (life) does not relate to the non-existent. The answer explains that here 'thing' is used in its linguistic sense (al-ma'na al-lughawi), which is an absolute term covering both existent and non-existent. Alternatively, if the technical meaning is intended, then the absence of relation to the non-existent is understood even more strongly (bi bab awla). Thus the expression is defended.

Key Terms
شيء
معنى لغوي
معنى اصطلاحي
معدوم
موجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'shay'' always has its technical meaning in kalam (i.e., existent).
Correction: In this passage, 'shay'' is used in its linguistic sense, meaning 'anything' or 'matter', covering both existent and non-existent. Kalam scholars often shift between linguistic and technical meanings depending on context.

Checkpoint

A) Because it implies the attribute relates to nothing at all
B) Because the word 'shay'' is too vague
C) Because the word 'shay'' usually means an existent, giving the wrong impression
D) Because the phrase is grammatically incorrect

Key Takeaway
The word 'shay'' can be used in its linguistic or technical sense; kalam arguments often rely on context to determine which is meant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

When you encounter a theological point that seems confusing or contradictory, do you quickly reject it, or do you, like the scholars here, consider that the words might be used in a different sense? What will you do next time you feel confused?

The Grammatical Rule for 'Ma'nawiyya'
Al-Bajuri explains the grammatical rule for forming 'ma'nawiyya' from 'ma'ani'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'ma'nawiyya' is used instead of 'ma'aniyya' based on the standard Arabic nisba rule for plural nouns.

Core Idea
The nisba to a plural uses the singular unless the plural is a proper noun.

Al-Bajuri explains a subtle grammatical point that affects a key term in kalam. The term 'ma'nawiyya' (attributes of meaning) is derived from 'ma'ani' (meanings). But why not 'ma'aniyya'? The answer lies in a standard Arabic rule for forming relative adjectives (nisba) from plural nouns. This passage unpacks that rule, addressing an objection and clarifying related Arabic morphology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point
Read the passage and note that 'ma'nawiyya' is a nisba to 'ma'ani'. The objection says one would expect 'ma'aniyya' instead. Understand the problem.
The nisba is an adjective ending in 'iyy' meaning 'related to'.
2
Grasp the rule
The answer cites a rule from al-Khulasa: when forming a nisba to a plural, use the singular form of the noun. Understand why this rule applies here.
The exception is when the plural has become a proper noun, like 'al-Ansar'.
3
Examine the example and exception
Al-Ajhuri gives the example of 'al-Ansar' (a proper noun for two tribes) where the nisba is 'Ansari' (using the plural because it resembles a singular). Compare with 'ma'ani' which is not a proper noun.
4
Apply the manqus rule
The taqrirat adds another layer: 'ma'ani' is a manqus noun (ending with ya') of five letters. Ibn 'Aqil's rule says a fifth ya' must be deleted in nisba, not changed to waw. This confirms the form 'ma'nawiyya'.
The ya' in 'ma'ani' is fifth after the alif, so deletion is obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتٍ مَعْنَوِيَّةً) نِسْبَةً للمعاني؛ لأنها تلازِمُها. فإن قيل: مقتضى النسبة إلى المعاني أن يقال مُعَانَوِيَّةٌ لا معنويةً. أجيب: بأن القاعدةَ أنه إذا نُسِبَ إلى الجمع لا يُذْكَرُ لفظه، بل لفظ المفرد، إلا إذا أَشْبَة لفظه لفظ المفرد، قال في "الخلاصة": وَالْوَاحِدَ اذْكُرْ نَاسِباً لِلْجَمْعِ مَا لَمْ يُشَابِه وَاحِداً بِالْوَضْعِ. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: إِلَّا إِذا أَشْبَهَ لَفْظُهُ لَفْظَ الْمُفْرَدِ) بأن جعل علماً بالغلبة مثلاً، كالأنصار علماً بالغلبة على الأوس والخزرج، فيقال في النسبة إليه: أنصاري. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبايي. (قوله: فَإِنْ قِيلَ: مُقْتَضَى النِّسْبَةِ إِلَى الْمَعَانِي أَنْ يُقَالَ: مُعَانَوِيَّةٌ) في الدَّسُوقِي: إن مقتضى النسبة إلى المعاني أن يقال: مَعَانِيَّةً .اهـ. ولعله الواقع بدليل قوله في "الخلاصة": : وَالْأَلِفَ الْجَائِرَ أَرْبَعاً أَزِلْ كَذَاكَ يَا الْمَنْقُوصِ خَامِساً عُزِلْ. قال ابن عَقِيل في شرحه وأشار بقوله : وكذاك يا المنصوص... إلخ إلى أنه إذا نُسِبَ إلى المنقوص، فإن كانت ياؤه ثالثةً؛ قُلِبَتْ واواً وفُتِحَ ما قبلها، نحو: شَجَوِيٌّ في شجي، وإن كانت رابعةٌ حُذِفَتْ، نحو: قاضي في قاض، وقد تُقْلَبُ ،واواً، نحو: قاضوي، وإن كانت خامسة فصاعداً، وَجَبَ حَذْفُها، كمتعدي في متعدّ، ومستعلي في مستعل اهـ. وما نحن فيه من قبيل ما كانت ياؤه خامسةً، فيجب حَذْفُها لا قَلْبُها واواً. تأمل.
His saying: 'They are called ma'nawiyya attributes' – attribution to ma'ani, because they are inseparable from them. If it is said: The requirement of attribution to ma'ani is that it should be said mu'aniyya, not ma'nawiyya. It is answered: That the rule is that when attributing to a plural, its word is not mentioned, rather the word of the singular, unless its word resembles the word of the singular. He said in al-Khulasa: 'mention the singular attributing to the plural, as long as it does not resemble a singular by coinage.' Marginal note of al-'Allama Ahmad al-Ajhuri: his saying: 'unless its word resembles the word of the singular' – such as when it is made a proper noun by predominant usage, like al-Ansar as a proper noun for al-Aws and al-Khazraj, so in attribution to it one says Ansari. Taqrirat of al-'Allama Muhammad al-Ansari: his saying: 'If it is said: the requirement of attribution to ma'ani is that it should be said mu'aniyya' – in al-Dasuqi: the requirement of attribution to ma'ani is that it should be said ma'aniyya. End, and it is likely the actual correct form, as evidenced by his statement in al-Khulasa: 'and the alif that is irregular, if four, remove it; likewise, O al-manqus, remove the fifth.' Ibn 'Aqil said in his commentary: he indicated by his saying 'and likewise, O al-manqus...' etc. that when attributing to a manqus noun, if its ya' is third, it is changed to waw and what precedes it is opened, like shajawi in shaji; if it is fourth, it is deleted, like qadi in qad, and it may be changed to waw, like qadawi; and if it is fifth or more, its deletion is obligatory, like muta'addi in muta'ad, and musta'li in musta'l. End. And our case is of the type where its ya' is fifth, so its deletion is obligatory, not its change to waw. Consider carefully.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical explanation of why the nisba (attributive adjective) form 'ma'nawiyya' is used instead of 'ma'aniyya' when referring to the derived attributes (sifat ma'nawiyya). The author begins by noting that 'ma'nawiyya' is an attribution to 'ma'ani' (plural of 'ma'na'), because these attributes are inseparable from the attributes of meaning (sifat al-ma'ani). An objection is raised: the normal rule for nisba to a plural is to use the plural form, so one would expect 'mu'aniyya' or 'ma'aniyya'. The answer invokes a rule from Arabic grammar stated in 'al-Khulasa': when forming a nisba to a plural, you use the singular form unless the plural has become a proper noun by predominant usage (like 'al-Ansar' for the tribes of Aws and Khazraj). The marginal note from al-Ajhuri gives that example. Then the taqrirat of al-Ansari cites al-Dasuqi's suggestion that 'ma'aniyya' might be the correct form, supported by another verse from 'al-Khulasa' about the alif that is irregular. This leads to a detailed explanation from Ibn 'Aqil's commentary on al-Khulasa about the nisba to manqus nouns (ending with ya'). The rule: for three-letter roots, the ya' becomes waw; for four, it is deleted but can also become waw; for five or more, deletion is obligatory. In the case of 'ma'ani' (which has a fifth-letter ya' after the alif), deletion is required, yielding 'ma'nawiyya' (with the alif and the ya' removed, and the waw? Actually the process: 'ma'ani' is plural of 'ma'na'; the nisba to the singular 'ma'na' yields 'ma'nawiyy' (since 'ma'na' ends with alif maqsura? Actually 'ma'na' is a noun with alif maqsura, so nisba makes it 'ma'nawiyy'). The author's use of the rule about manqus suggests that 'ma'ani' is treated as a manqus with a fifth-letter ya' after alif, so the ya' is deleted and the alif irregular leads to 'ma'nawiyya'. The passage ends with 'consider carefully' (tammal), inviting reflection. Thus the lesson provides a thorough example of how Arabic grammatical rules apply to theological terminology.

معان (ma'ani)
معنوية (ma'nawiyya)
جمع (jam')
مفرد (mufrad)
منقوص (manqus)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'ma'nawiyya' is an irregular form unique to theological terminology.
Correction: It follows the standard nisba rule: use singular when attributing to a plural, and the manqus rule requires deletion of the fifth ya'.

Checkpoint
Why is the term 'ma'nawiyya' used instead of 'ma'aniyya'?
A) Because it follows the rule that nisba to a plural uses the singular.
B) Because 'ma'ani' is a proper noun.
C) Because the rule is to always use the plural form.
D) Because the ya' is fifth and must be changed to waw.

Key Takeaway
The term 'ma'nawiyya' follows the standard Arabic nisba rule: when attributing to a plural, use the singular form unless the plural is a proper noun.

How can you apply this patience to other areas of your deen, such as understanding Quranic verses that initially confuse you?
?

Why Are They Called Attributive Attributes? A Linguistic Defense
Al-Bajuri defines 'ṣifāt ma'nawiyya' and defends its linguistic form against an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic rule that justifies the term 'ma'nawiyya' for the attributive attributes.

Core Idea
The name 'ma'nawiyya' follows a standard Arabic nisba rule, not a grammatical error.

In this passage, al-Bajuri defines what is meant by 'attributive attributes' (ṣifāt ma'nawiyya) and then answers a linguistic objection. The objector claims the term should be 'mu'ānawiyya', but al-Bajuri invokes a classical Arabic rule of attribution to plural nouns. This lesson unpacks both the definition and the linguistic defense.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the definition
Read the opening phrase: 'they are called attributive attributes as a relation to the meanings because they are concomitant with them.' Understand that the attributes are named after the meanings they relate to.
The term 'ma'nawiyya' is derived from 'ma'nā' (meaning) via the rule.
2
Identify the objection
Notice the objection: since 'ma'ānī' is a plural, the nisba should be 'mu'ānawiyya'. Why is it 'ma'nawiyya' instead?
3
Learn the rule
The answer gives the rule: when forming a nisba from a plural, use the singular form unless the plural word resembles a singular in coinage.
This rule is standard Arabic grammar, quoted from al-Khulāṣa.
4
Apply the rule
Since 'ma'ānī' does not resemble a singular, the singular 'ma'nā' is used, giving 'ma'nawiyya'. Confirm with the example of 'al-Anṣār' where the plural is used because it resembles a singular.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتٍ مَعْنَوِيَّةً) نِسْبَةً للمعاني؛ لأنها تلازِمُها. فإن قيل: مقتضى النسبة إلى المعاني أن يقال مُعَانَوِيَّةٌ لا معنويةً. أجيب: بأن القاعدةَ أنه إذا نُسِبَ إلى الجمع لا يُذْكَرُ لفظه، بل لفظ المفرد، إلا إذا أَشْبَهَ لفظه لفظ المفرد، قال في 'الخلاصة': وَالْوَاحِدَ اذْكُرْ نَاسِباً لِلْجَمْعِ مَا لَمْ يُشَابِه وَاحِداً بِالْوَضْع. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: إِلَّا إِذا أَشْبَهَ لَفْظُهُ لَفْظَ الْمُفْرَدِ) بأن جعل علماً بالغلبة مثلاً، كالأنصار علماً بالغلبة على الأوس والخزرج، فيقال في النسبة إليه: أنصاري.
(His saying: 'they are called attributive attributes (ṣifāt ma'nawiyya)') as a relation (nisba) to the meanings (al-ma'ānī) because they are concomitant with them. For if it is said: The requirement of the relation to the plural (al-ma'ānī) is that it should be said mu'ānawiyya, not ma'nawiyya. It is answered: Because the rule is that when one attributes to a plural, its word is not mentioned, but rather the word of the singular, unless its word resembles the word of the singular. He said in al-Khulāṣa: 'And mention the singular when attributing to a plural, as long as it does not resemble a singular in coinage.' Gloss of al-ʿAllāma Aḥmad al-Ujhūrī: (His saying: 'unless its word resembles the word of the singular') such as when it is made a proper noun (ʿalaman bi al-ghalaba) for example, like al-Anṣār as a proper noun by preponderance for al-Aws and al-Khazraj, so in the attribution to it one says Anṣārī.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'ṣifāt ma'nawiyya' (attributive attributes) and addresses a linguistic objection. Al-Bajuri explains that these attributes are called 'ma'nawiyya' because they are relative (nisba) to the 'ma'ānī' (meanings), which are the seven essential attributes (power, will, etc.), and they are concomitant (mulāzima) with them. An objector argues that the correct form of the adjective from the plural 'ma'ānī' should be 'mu'ānawiyya' not 'ma'nawiyya'. The answer invokes the Arabic grammatical rule: when forming a relative adjective (nisba) from a plural, one should use the singular form unless the plural word resembles a singular in its coinage (e.g., if it has become a proper noun). This is supported by a verse from the grammar text al-Khulāṣa. Al-Ajhuri's gloss gives an example: the plural 'al-Anṣār' when used as a proper noun for the tribes of al-Aws and al-Khazraj, the nisba is 'Anṣārī' (using the plural form) because it resembles a singular. Since 'ma'ānī' does not resemble a singular, the nisba uses the singular 'ma'nā', giving 'ma'nawiyya'.

Key Terms
صفات معنوية
نسبة إلى المعاني
ملازمة
قاعدة النسبة إلى الجمع
لغة عربية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'ma'nawiyya' is a grammatical mistake because it should be derived from the plural form 'ma'ānī'.
Correction: According to Arabic grammar, when forming a relative adjective from a plural that does not resemble a singular, the singular form is used, making 'ma'nawiyya' correct.

Checkpoint
Why is the term 'ma'nawiyya' used instead of 'mu'ānawiyya' for the attributive attributes?
A) Because it is easier to pronounce
B) Because the rule of nisba to a plural uses the singular unless the plural resembles a singular
C) Because the word 'ma'ānī' is not a real plural
D) Because al-Bajuri made a mistake

Key Takeaway
The term 'ṣifāt ma'nawiyya' is linguistically valid because Arabic grammar dictates using the singular form when forming a relative adjective from a plural that does not resemble a singular.

?

Nisba to Plurals of Defective Nouns: The Fifth Ya' Rule
Al-Anbābī elaborates on the nisba rule for plurals with a ya' of more than four letters, citing Ibn ʿAqīl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how to form nisba from defective nouns when the ya' is the fifth letter or more, specifically that deletion is obligatory.

Core Idea
When the ya' of a defective noun is fifth or higher in nisba, deletion is obligatory.

This lesson examines a specific linguistic rule from al-Anbābī's annotations. The issue arises when forming nisba from a plural like ma'ānī. Should one follow the singular pattern or a special rule for defective nouns? The passage presents the rule as codified by Ibn ʿAqīl.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note the key terms: manqūs (defective noun) and ya' (the letter yā).
The passage references al-Khulāṣa and Ibn ʿAqīl's commentary.
2
Identify the rule for each ya' position
From Ibn ʿAqīl's explanation, note the three cases: if the ya' is third, change to wāw; if fourth, delete (or optionally change to wāw); if fifth or more, delete obligatorily.
Pay attention to the verbs: 'qulibat' (changed), 'ḥudhifat' (deleted), 'wajaba ḥadhfuha' (obligatory deletion).
3
Apply the rule to 'ma'ānī'
Determine the position of the ya' in 'ma'ānī'. The letters are mīm, ʿayn, alif, nūn, yā — so the yā is fifth. According to the rule, it must be deleted, yielding 'ma'āniyya'.
This confirms the correctness of the form 'ma'āniyya' over 'mu'ānawiyya'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي (قوله: فَإِنْ قِيلَ: مُقْتَضَى النِّسْبَةِ إِلَى الْمَعَانِي أَنْ يُقَالَ: مُعَانَوِيَّةٌ) في الدَّسُوقِي: إن مقتضى النسبة إلى المعاني أن يقال: مَعَانِيَّةً .اهـ. ولعله الواقع بدليل قوله في 'الخلاصة': وَالْأَلِفَ الْجَائِرَ أَرْبَعاً أَزِلْ كَذَاكَ يَا الْمَنْقُوصِ خَامِساً عُزِلْ قال ابن عَقِيل في شرحه وأشار بقوله : وكذاك يا المنصوص... إلخ إلى أنه إذا نُسِبَ إلى المنقوص، فإن كانت ياؤه ثالثةً؛ قُلِبَتْ واواً وفُتِحَ ما قبلها، نحو: شَجَوِيٌّ في شجي، وإن كانت رابعةٌ حُذِفَتْ، نحو: قاضي في قاض، وقد تُقْلَبُ واواً، نحو: قاضوي، وإن كانت خامسة فصاعداً، وَجَبَ حَذْفُها، كمتعدي في متعدّ، ومستعلي في مستعل اهـ. وما نحن فيه من قبيل ما كانت ياؤه خامسةً، فيجب حَذْفُها لا قَلْبُها واواً. تأمل.
Annotations of the ʿAllāma Muḥammad al-Anbābī: (His saying: 'For if it is said: The requirement of the relation to the meanings is that it should be said muʿānawiyya') in al-Dasūqī: 'The requirement of the relation to the meanings is that it should be said maʿāniyya.' End quote. And perhaps it is the reality, as evidenced by his saying in al-Khulāṣa: 'And the irregular alif of four, remove it, likewise the ya' of the defective noun of five is removed.' Ibn ʿAqīl said in his commentary: 'And he indicated by his saying "and likewise ya' of the defective" that when attributing to a defective noun (ism manqūṣ), if its ya' is third, it is changed to a wāw and what precedes it is fatha, e.g., shajawī from shajī; if it is fourth, it is deleted, e.g., qāḍī becomes qāḍin, and sometimes it is changed to wāw, e.g., qāḍawī; if it is fifth or more, its deletion is obligatory, like mutaʿaddī becomes mutaʿadd, and mustaʿlī becomes mustaʿal.' End quote. And what we are dealing with is of the type where the ya' is fifth, so deletion is obligatory, not changing to a wāw. Reflect.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an extended linguistic analysis of the nisba rule for defective nouns (al-manqūṣ). Al-Anbābī begins by noting an alternative view from al-Dasūqī that the proper form from 'maʿānī' should be 'maʿāniyya' (with deletion of the alif). He then cites a verse from al-Khulāṣa about the treatment of alif and ya' in nisba, and Ibn ʿAqīl's commentary explains the rules: if the ya' is third, change to wāw; if fourth, delete (or optionally change); if fifth or more, obligatory deletion. Since 'maʿānī' has a ya' that is fifth (the letters are mīm, ʿayn, alif, nūn, yā'), the ya' must be deleted, resulting in 'maʿāniyya'. This supports al-Dasūqī's view. The lesson emphasizes that the correct nisba from 'maʿānī' is 'maʿāniyya', not 'muʿānawiyya' nor 'maʿnawiyya'? Actually earlier the view was 'maʿnawiyya' from singular. This shows there is a debate. However, this lesson solely presents al-Anbābī's analysis of the rule.

Key Terms
نسبة إلى الجمع
منقوص
الياء الخامسة
الخلاصة
ابن عقيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the nisba from a plural always uses the singular form or that the ya' should be changed to wāw regardless of position.
Correction: For defective nouns, the treatment of the ya' depends on its position: third ya' is changed to wāw, fourth ya' is deleted (or optionally wāw), but fifth or more requires obligatory deletion.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn ʿAqīl, what must be done to the ya' of a defective noun when it is the fifth letter or more in nisba?
A) Change it to a wāw
B) Keep it unchanged
C) Delete it obligatorily
D) Add an alif before it

Key Takeaway
The nisba from a defective noun with a fifth ya' requires obligatory deletion of the ya', not conversion to wāw.

The Pronoun Reference and the Concept of Non-Existence
Al-Bajuri's grammatical and logical analysis of the pronoun and non-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Bajuri's grammatical parsing of the phrase 'wa hiya' and his logical distinction between non-existence and 'not existence', including the related glosses on utmost difference and mental consideration.

Core Idea
Non-existence is more specific than 'not existence'.

Al-Bajuri begins by dissecting the grammatical structure of the phrase 'wa hiya', clarifying the subject and predicate. He then delves into the logical relationship between existence and non-existence, showing that non-existence is a subset of a broader category. The subsequent glosses by al-Ajhuri and al-Anbabi further refine the concepts of opposition and mental consideration. This passage combines grammar, logic, and theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the grammatical and logical terms.
The passage includes two glosses – try to separate the main text from the glosses.
2
Identify the grammatical analysis
Al-Bajuri says the pronoun 'hiya' is the subject, and 'al-‘adam' (non-existence) along with its conjuncts is the predicate. Understand this basic parsing.
This sets the stage for the logical discussion.
3
Understand the logical opposition
The opposition between existence and non-existence is like that between a thing and a more specific version of its contradictory. The contradictory of existence is 'la wujud', which includes non-existence, mental considerations, and the intermediate. So non-existence is more specific than 'la wujud'.
This clarifies the terminology.
4
Examine the glosses
Read the gloss on 'ghayat al-khilaf' (utmost difference) as mutual exclusion, and the gloss on 'al-amr al-i‘tibari' (mental consideration) which warns about confusing truth and description.
These glosses provide further precision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَهِيَ) لا يخفى أن الضمير مبتدأ، وقوله: (العدم) وما عُطِفَ عليه خبر، والتقابل بين الوجود والعدم من التقابل بين الشيء والأخص من نقيضه؛ لأن نقيض الوجود: لا وُجُودَ ، وهو يشمل العدمَ والأمر الاعتباري والواسِطَةَ على القول بها، فالعدمُ أخصُّ من لا وجود الذي هو نقيضُ الوجود. (حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري) (قوله: غَايَةُ الْخِلَافِ المراد بها التنافي بينهما، فقوله: (لا يجتمعان) تفسير لها، وخرج بهذا القيد الخلافان كالقيام والضحك، فإن بينهما أصل الخلاف، لا غايته لإمكان اجتماعهما. (تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي) (وقوله: فَلَا تَكُونُ ضِدّاً لِغَيْرهَا أي: لا ينبغي ذلك؛ لأنه اللائق بالأدب؛ لأنه خاص بالحادث. (قوله: وَالْأَمْرَ الْاِعْتِباري) دخلَ فيه الوجود، فإن الوجودَ يَتَّصِفُ بلا وجود، فيقال: الوجودُ لا وُجُودَ له، بل إنما هو حالةٌ لها ثُبوت فقط. وفيه: أن المراد: الصدقُ لا الاتِّصَافُ، ولا يصدق على الوجود لا وجود فالحق أن المراد: الأمرُ الاعتباري غير النفسي ليخرج الوجود، وإلا؛ لَزِمَ صِدْقُ نقيض الشيء عليه. تأمل.
His statement: 'And they' — it is not hidden that the pronoun is subject, and his statement: 'non-existence' and what is conjoined to it is predicate. And the opposition between existence and non-existence is of the type of opposition between a thing and the more specific of its contradictory, because the contradictory of existence is 'not existence', and it includes non-existence, the mental consideration, and the intermediate [state] according to the position that affirms it. So non-existence is more specific than 'not existence' which is the contradictory of existence. (Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri): His statement: 'Utmost difference' means by it the mutual exclusion between them, so his statement: 'they do not coexist' is an interpretation of it. And by this restriction, differences like standing and laughing are excluded, for between them there is basic difference, not utmost difference, due to the possibility of their coexistence. (Annotations of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi): And his statement: 'So it is not an opposite to other than it' means that is not appropriate, because it is befitting good manners, since it is specific to the temporal. His statement: 'And the mental consideration' includes existence, for existence is described as 'not existence', so it is said: existence has no existence, rather it is only a state that has subsistence only. And in it: that what is meant is truth (صدق) not description (اتصاف), and 'not existence' is not true of existence, so the truth is that what is meant is the mental consideration other than the psychic, to exclude existence; otherwise, the truth of the contradictory of the thing would follow from it. Ponder.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and logical analysis. Al-Bajuri first parses the phrase 'wa hiya' (and they), identifying the pronoun as subject and 'al-‘adam' (non-existence) as predicate. He then explains the opposition between existence and non-existence: it is a relation between a thing and a more specific version of its contradictory. The contradictory of existence is 'la wujud' (not existence), which includes non-existence, mental considerations, and the intermediate state. Non-existence is more specific than 'la wujud'. The glosses then provide further details: al-Ajhuri explains 'ghayat al-khilaf' (utmost difference) as mutual exclusion, noting that basic differences like standing and laughing are excluded because they can coexist. Al-Anbabi comments that the author's phrase 'fa la takun ḍiddan li-ghayriha' means it is not fitting for God's attributes to be called 'opposite' to others, as that is specific to temporal things. Finally, al-Anbabi discusses 'al-amr al-i‘tibari' (mental consideration), arguing that existence itself can be described as 'la wujud' in a certain sense, but this is not actual description but truth-value, and mental considerations exclude psychic entities. He cautions against misunderstanding.

Correction: Al-Bajuri shows non-existence is more specific; 'not existence' includes non-existence, mental considerations, and the intermediate state.

D) They are opposites

Key Takeaway
Non-existence is a narrower concept than 'not existence', and careful grammatical and logical analysis is essential for precise theological discourse.

The Meaning of 'ضد' and the Classification of Opposites
Explains the term 'ضد' as applied to the twenty attributes and their opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Sanusi used the term 'أضداد' only for the opposites of God's attributes and not vice versa, and the distinction between the linguistic and technical meanings of 'ضد'.

Core Idea
The term 'ضد' has a broad linguistic sense and a narrow technical sense; only some of the twenty opposites are true contraries.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary clarifies the term 'ضد' as used by al-Sanusi. It addresses why the author applied 'opposites' only to the attributes' counterparts and not vice versa, and distinguishes between linguistic and technical definitions. The explanation is essential for understanding the classification of the twenty opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the objection (ويُحث فيه) and how it is resolved.
2
Identify why Sanusi did not reverse the term
The passage explains that God's attributes are eternal, so they cannot be called 'opposites'. Find this reasoning.
3
Understand the objection about two-sided contrariety
The objection says contrariety is a two-sided relation, so calling something a 'ضد' does not imply origination. See how the commentator responds.
The resolution: 'ضد' can be used linguistically for both eternal and originated.
4
Distinguish linguistic vs. technical sense
The commentator explicitly says the intended meaning is the linguistic sense of absolute opposition. In the technical sense, only some are true contraries.
Technical definition: two existent things extremely opposed, cannot coexist, may both be absent (e.g., black and white).
5
Note the subtypes among the twenty
This sets the stage for further classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَهِيَ أَضْدَادُ الْعِشْرِينَ الْأُولَى أي: الأَوَّل ضد للأول، والثاني للثاني، وهكذا على الترتيب المتقدّم في الواجبات وأطلق المصنف الأضداد على المقابل لصفاته تعالى، ولم يَعْكِس؛ لأن صفاته تعالى قديمة، فلا تكون ضدّاً لغيرها. هكذا يُؤْخَذُ من كلام الشيخ يس. ويُحِثَ فيه: بأن التضاد: نسبة من الجانبين فكلُّ منهما ضِدُّ للآخر، ولا يلزمُ من ذلك كَوْنُ صفاته تعالى حادثةً ؛ لأن الضدَّ كما يُطْلَقُ على الحادث؛ يُطْلَقُ على القديم والمراد بالضد هنا: المعنى اللغوي، وهو مُطْلَقُ المُنَافي، وإلا؛ فليست هذه العشرون كلُّها أضداداً للعشرين الأولى بالمعنى الاصطلاحي؛ لأن الضدين في الاصطلاح هما الأمران الوجوديَّان اللذان بينهما غايةُ الخلاف، لا يجتمعان، وقد يرتفعان كالسواد والبياض وليست هذه العشرون كلُّها كذلك، بل بعضُها ضد، وبعضها نقيض، وبعضُها مُسَاءٍ للنقيض، وبعضُها أخصُّ من النقيض كما ستقف عليه إن شاء الله تعالى.)
His saying: 'And they are the opposites of the first twenty' means: the first is the opposite of the first, the second of the second, and so on in the order previously mentioned in the necessary attributes. And the author applied the term 'opposites' to what is opposite to His attributes, may He be exalted, and did not reverse, because His attributes, may He be exalted, are eternal, so they cannot be opposites to other than them. This is taken from the words of Shaykh Yas. And it is contested in it: that contrariety is a relation from both sides, so each of them is an opposite of the other, and it does not necessarily follow from that that His attributes, may He be exalted, are originated, because the term 'opposite' as applied to the originated is also applied to the eternal. And what is meant by 'opposite' here is the linguistic meaning, which is absolute opposition. Otherwise, these twenty are not all opposites of the first twenty in the technical sense, because technically the two opposites are the two existent things between which there is extreme difference, they do not coexist, and they may both be absent, like blackness and whiteness. And these twenty are not all like that. Rather, some of them are opposites, some are negations, some are equivalents of the negation, and some are more specific than the negation, as you will come to know, God willing.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the term 'ضد' (opposite/contrary) as used by al-Sanusi in his enumeration of the twenty attributes of God and their opposites. The commentator begins by clarifying that the phrase 'وهي أضداد العشرين الأولى' means that the first opposite corresponds to the first attribute, the second to the second, and so on, following the same order previously given for the necessary attributes. He then notes that al-Sanusi used the plural 'أضداد' for the opposites of God's attributes, but did not reverse (i.e., he did not call the attributes 'أضداد' for their opposites), because God's attributes are eternal and therefore cannot be considered opposites of anything else. This point is supported by reference to Shaykh Yas. The commentator then raises an objection: contrariety is a two-sided relation, so each of two contraries is an opposite of the other. Therefore, applying the term 'ضد' to an attribute does not imply that the attribute is originated, because the term can be used in a linguistic sense for both eternal and originated things. The intended meaning here is the linguistic sense of absolute opposition. If the technical sense were meant, then the twenty opposites would not all be true contraries in the technical sense. Technically, two contraries are two existent things that are extremely opposed, cannot coexist, and may both be absent, such as blackness and whiteness. The twenty opposites include some that are true contraries, some that are negations, some that are equivalents of negation, and some that are more specific than negation. This sets the stage for a detailed classification later.

أضداد
التضاد
المعنى اللغوي
المعنى الاصطلاحي
نقيض
مساءٍ للنقيض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Calling something a 'ضد' (opposite) implies it is originated (hadith).
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'ضد' can be used in a linguistic sense for both eternal and originated things, so applying it to an eternal attribute does not imply origination.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author (al-Sanusi) use 'أضداد' for the opposites of God's attributes and not the reverse?
A) Because God's attributes are eternal and cannot be contraries of other things.
B) Because the twenty attributes are too many.
C) Because the linguistic sense allows it.
D) Because the technical sense requires it.

Key Takeaway
The twenty opposites of God’s attributes include various logical relations, not all are true contraries in the technical sense, and the term 'ضد' is used here in its broad linguistic meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you use the word 'opposite' to describe something about Allah, do you unconsciously project human limitations onto Him? How can you train yourself to separate linguistic convenience from theological precision, starting with this lesson?
?
The passage shows that a single term can have multiple valid meanings depending on context. In your own understanding of Islam, are there areas where you have rigidly applied one meaning without considering the broader linguistic sense? What is the cost of that rigidity?
?

Extreme Difference as Mutual Exclusion
Al-Ajhuri glosses 'غاية الخلاف' in contrariety definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'غاية الخلاف' means mutual exclusion (التنافي) and how this qualification distinguishes true contraries from mere differences.

Core Idea
Extreme difference means mutual exclusion, not any difference.

Al-Sanusi defines contrariety using the phrase 'غاية الخلاف'. Al-Ajhuri clarifies that this refers to mutual exclusion, not extreme difference in degree. For example, standing and laughing can coexist, so they are not true opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the gloss on 'غاية الخلاف'
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note that 'غاية الخلاف' is interpreted as mutual exclusion (التنافي) and the phrase 'لا يجتمعان' is its explanation.
2
Examine the example of standing and laughing
These two have basic difference but not extreme difference because they can coexist (e.g., a person standing and laughing). This shows the importance of the qualification.
3
Reflect on the broader implication
Understanding this distinction helps correctly identify what counts as a true opposite in kalam, especially for Divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
(قوله: غَايَةُ الْخِلَافِ المراد بها التنافي بينهما، فقوله: (لا يجتمعان) تفسير لها، وخرج بهذا القيد الخلافان كالقيام والضحك، فإن بينهما أصل الخلاف، لا غايته لإمكان اجتماعهما.
تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي.
(وقوله: فَلَا تَكُونُ ضِدّاً لِغَيْرهَا أي: لا ينبغي ذلك؛ لأنه اللائق بالأدب؛ لأنه خاص بالحادث. (قوله: وَالْأَمْرَ الْاِعْتِباري) دخلَ فيه الوجود، فإن الوجودَ يَتَّصِفُ بلا وجود، فيقال: الوجودُ لا وُجُودَ له، بل إنما هو حالةٌ لها ثُبوت فقط. وفيه: أن المراد: الصدقُ لا الاتِّصَافُ، ولا يصدق على الوجود لا وجود فالحق أن المراد: الأمرُ الاعتباري غير النفسي ليدخل الوجود، وإلا ; لَزِمَ صِدْقُ نقيض الشيء عليه. تأمل.
Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri:
His saying: 'Extreme difference' – what is meant is the mutual exclusion between the two. So his saying: 'they do not coexist' is an interpretation of it. And by this qualification are excluded the two differences like standing and laughing, for between them is a basic difference, not its extreme, because they can coexist.
Notations of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi:
And His saying: 'so they are not opposites to other than them' – meaning it is not appropriate, because it is fitting for etiquette, because it is specific to the originated.
His saying: 'and the mental consideration' – existence enters into it, because existence is described by non-existence, so it is said: existence has no existence, but rather it is a state that has only subsistence. And regarding it: that what is meant is truth, not attribution, and 'non-existence' is not true of existence. So the truth is that what is meant is the mental consideration other than the self-subsistent, to include existence, otherwise the contradictory of a thing would be true of it. Reflect.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a set of three glosses on specific phrases from al-Sanusi's text, provided by two scholars. The first gloss, from al-Ajhuri, explains the phrase 'غاية الخلاف' (extreme difference) in the definition of contrariety. He states that what is meant by 'extreme difference' is the mutual exclusion between the two things, so the statement 'they do not coexist' is an interpretation of it. With this qualification, examples like standing and laughing are excluded because although there is a basic difference, they can coexist. The second gloss, from al-Anbabi, explains the phrase 'فلا تكون ضداً لغيرها' (so they are not opposites to other than them). It means that it is not appropriate to consider God's attributes as opposites, because that would be against etiquette, as the term 'ضد' is specifically associated with originated things. The third gloss, also from al-Anbabi, explains 'والأمر الاعتباري' (the mental consideration). It notes that existence itself can be included under this term, because existence can be described by non-existence in a certain sense—existence is a state that has only subsistence (ثبوت) and not existence in the usual sense. The gloss then clarifies that the intended meaning here is truth (صدق), not attribution (اتصاف), and that the phrase 'لا وجود' (non-existence) does not truly apply to existence. Therefore, the correct understanding is that 'الأمر الاعتباري' is the mental consideration that is not self-subsistent (غير النفسي), in order to include existence. Otherwise, if existence were considered a self-subsistent mental object, then the contradictory of a thing would be true of it, which is a problem worthy of reflection.

Key Terms
غاية الخلاف
التنافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'غاية الخلاف' means extreme difference in degree or intensity.
Correction: It actually means mutual exclusion, i.e., impossibility of coexistence.

Checkpoint
What does 'غاية الخلاف' mean according to al-Ajhuri?
A) Extreme difference in degree.
B) Mutual exclusion.
C) Identity.
D) Similarity.

Key Takeaway
'غاية الخلاف' means mutual exclusion, not any difference; true opposites are those that cannot coexist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a belief or habit in your life that you consider 'just different' from Islamic teachings. Could it actually be a 'غاية الخلاف'—something that cannot coexist with true faith? What would it cost you to examine it honestly?
?
This lesson shows that not every difference is a contradiction. Where in your relationships or community do you treat minor differences as if they are mutually exclusive, causing unnecessary division? What would change if you applied this distinction?
?
The source uses logical precision to guard against error. How often do you let emotions or assumptions blur the line between what is merely different and what is truly contradictory to your deen? Can you name one area where you need to be more precise?

Why God's Attributes Are Not Called Opposites
Al-Anbabi glosses 'فلا تكون ضداً لغيرها' from Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'ضد' (opposite) is not applied to God's attributes, because it is specific to originated beings and a matter of etiquette.

Core Idea
God's attributes are not called 'ضد' because that term implies origination.

Al-Sanusi says God's attributes are not opposites to other things. Al-Anbabi explains this is because it is inappropriate etiquette and because 'ضد' is specific to created beings. This lesson unpacks the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the gloss on 'فلا تكون ضداً لغيرها'
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the phrase 'لا ينبغي ذلك' (it is not appropriate).
2
Identify the two reasons given
First, it's a matter of proper etiquette (اللائق بالأدب). Second, the term 'ضد' is specific to originated beings (خاص بالحادث).
3
Reflect on why this matters
Avoiding such terms for God maintains His transcendence and uniqueness, preventing anthropomorphism.

Source Text
